     <p>The <b>University of Chicago</b> (<b>U of C</b>, <b>UChicago</b>, or simply <b>Chicago</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. The university consists of the <a href="/wiki/College_of_the_University_of_Chicago" title="College of the University of Chicago">College of the University of Chicago</a>, various graduate programs and interdisciplinary committees organized into four divisions, six <a href="/wiki/Professional_school" title="Professional school">professional schools</a>, and a school of <a href="/wiki/Continuing_education" title="Continuing education">continuing education</a>. The university enrolls approximately 5,000 students in the College and about 15,000 students overall. The University of Chicago is consistently ranked among the world's top 10 universities and is considered one of the world's most prestigious schools.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>University of Chicago scholars have played a major role in the development of various academic disciplines, including: the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_school_of_economics" title="Chicago school of economics">Chicago school of economics</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_school_(sociology)" title="Chicago school (sociology)">Chicago school of sociology</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Law_and_economics" title="Law and economics">law and economics</a> movement in legal analysis,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_school_(literary_criticism)" title="Chicago school (literary criticism)">Chicago school of literary criticism</a>, the Chicago school of religion,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> the school of political science known as <a href="/wiki/Behavioralism" title="Behavioralism">behavioralism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> and in the physics leading to <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Pile_1" title="Chicago Pile 1" class="mw-redirect">the world's first man-made, self-sustaining</a> <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reaction" title="Nuclear reaction">nuclear reaction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> The university is also home to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Press" title="University of Chicago Press">University of Chicago Press</a>, the largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_university_presses" title="List of university presses">university press</a> in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-press_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-press-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Chicago is affiliated with 87 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Laureates</a> (including 8 current faculty),<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> 49 <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholars" title="Rhodes Scholars" class="mw-redirect">Rhodes Scholars</a><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> and 9 <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medalists" title="Fields Medalists" class="mw-redirect">Fields Medalists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> It was founded by the <a href="/wiki/American_Baptist_Churches_USA" title="American Baptist Churches USA">American Baptist Education Society</a> with a donation from oil magnate and philanthropist <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller" title="John D. Rockefeller">John D. Rockefeller</a> and incorporated in 1890. <a href="/wiki/William_Rainey_Harper" title="William Rainey Harper">William Rainey Harper</a> became the university's first president in 1891, and the first classes were held in 1892.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_University_of_Chicago" title="History of the University of Chicago">History of the University of Chicago</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Uchicago_convocation_1894.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Uchicago_convocation_1894.jpg/250px-Uchicago_convocation_1894.jpg" width="250" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Uchicago_convocation_1894.jpg/375px-Uchicago_convocation_1894.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Uchicago_convocation_1894.jpg/500px-Uchicago_convocation_1894.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Uchicago_convocation_1894.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> An early 
        <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocation</a> ceremony at the University of Chicago
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding.E2.80.931910s">Founding?1910s</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Founding?1910s">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of Chicago was created and <a href="/wiki/Incorporation_(business)" title="Incorporation (business)">incorporated</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Mixed-sex_education" title="Mixed-sex education">coeducational</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> secular institution in 1890 by the <a href="/wiki/American_Baptist_Churches_USA" title="American Baptist Churches USA">American Baptist Education Society</a> and a donation from oil magnate and philanthropist <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller" title="John D. Rockefeller">John D. Rockefeller</a> on land donated by <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Field" title="Marshall Field">Marshall Field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> It emerged from a <a href="/wiki/Old_University_of_Chicago" title="Old University of Chicago">Baptist university of the same name</a> that had closed in 1886 due to financial difficulties. <a href="/wiki/William_Rainey_Harper" title="William Rainey Harper">William Rainey Harper</a> became the modern university's first president on July 1, 1891, and the first classes were held on October 1, 1892.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Booth_School_of_Business" title="University of Chicago Booth School of Business" class="mw-redirect">business school</a> was founded in 1898,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Law_School" title="University of Chicago Law School">law school</a> was founded in 1902.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Harper died in 1906,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> and was replaced by a series of three presidents whose tenures lasted until 1929.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> During this period, the <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Institute,_Chicago" title="Oriental Institute, Chicago" class="mw-redirect">Oriental Institute</a> was founded.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the 1890s, the University of Chicago, fearful that its vast resources would injure smaller schools by drawing away good students, affiliated with several regional colleges and universities, including <a href="/wiki/Des_Moines_College" title="Des Moines College">Des Moines College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kalamazoo_College" title="Kalamazoo College">Kalamazoo College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Butler_University" title="Butler University">Butler College</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stetson_University" title="Stetson University">Stetson University</a>. Under the terms of the affiliation, the schools were required to have courses of study comparable to those at the University of Chicago, to notify the university early of any contemplated faculty appointments or dismissals, to make no faculty appointment without the university's approval, and to send copies of examinations for suggestions. The University of Chicago agreed to confer a degree on any graduating senior from an affiliated school who made a grade of A for all four years and on any other graduate who took twelve weeks additional study at the University of Chicago. A student or faculty member of an affiliated school was entitled to free tuition at the University of Chicago, and Chicago students were eligible to attend an affiliated school on the same terms and receive credit for their work. The University of Chicago also agreed to provide affiliated schools with books and scientific apparatus and supplies at cost, to provide special instructors and lecturers without cost except travel expenses, and a copy of every book and journal published by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Press" title="University of Chicago Press">University of Chicago Press</a> was to be provided to the affiliated schools at no cost. The agreement provided that either party could terminate the affiliation on proper notice. Several University of Chicago professors disliked the program, as it involved uncompensated additional labor on their part, and also because they believed it cheapened the academic reputation of the University of Chicago. The program passed into history by 1910.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1920s.E2.80.931980s">1920s?1980s</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1920s?1980s">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 1929, the university's fifth president, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Maynard_Hutchins" title="Robert Maynard Hutchins">Robert Maynard Hutchins</a>, took office; the university underwent many changes during his 24-year tenure. Hutchins eliminated varsity football from the university in an attempt to emphasize academics over athletics,<sup id="cite_ref-hutchins_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hutchins-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> instituted the undergraduate college's liberal-arts curriculum known as the Common Core,<sup id="cite_ref-core_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-core-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> and organized the university's graduate work into its current<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (December 2011)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> four divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-hutchins_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hutchins-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1933, Hutchins proposed an unsuccessful plan to merge the University of Chicago and <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University" title="Northwestern University">Northwestern University</a> into a single university.<sup id="cite_ref-merger_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merger-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> During his term, the University of Chicago Hospitals (now called the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Medical_Center" title="University of Chicago Medical Center">University of Chicago Medical Center</a>) finished construction and enrolled its first medical students,<sup id="cite_ref-hospitalhistory_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hospitalhistory-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Committee_on_Social_Thought" title="Committee on Social Thought">Committee on Social Thought</a> was created.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:ChicagoPileTeam.png" class="image"><img alt="A group of people in suits standing in three rows on the steps in front of a stone building." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/ChicagoPileTeam.png/350px-ChicagoPileTeam.png" width="350" height="263" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1c/ChicagoPileTeam.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1c/ChicagoPileTeam.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:ChicagoPileTeam.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The University of Chicago team that worked on the production of the world's first man-made, self-sustaining nuclear reaction, including 
        <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Fermi" title="Enrico Fermi">Enrico Fermi</a> in the front row and 
        <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3_Szil%C3%A1rd" title="Le&oacute; Szil&aacute;rd">Le&oacute; Szil&aacute;rd</a> in the second.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Money that had been raised during the 1920s and financial backing from the <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Foundation" title="Rockefeller Foundation">Rockefeller Foundation</a> helped the school to survive through the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hutchins_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hutchins-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> During World War II, the university made important contributions to the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Project" title="Manhattan Project">Manhattan Project</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-manhattan_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-manhattan-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> The university was the site of the first isolation of <a href="/wiki/Plutonium" title="Plutonium">plutonium</a> and of the creation of the first artificial, self-sustained nuclear reaction by <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Fermi" title="Enrico Fermi">Enrico Fermi</a> in 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-manhattan_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-manhattan-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the early 1950s, student applications declined as a result of increasing crime and poverty in the Hyde Park neighborhood. In response, the university became a major sponsor of a controversial <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_Chicago#Urban_renewal" title="Hyde Park, Chicago">urban renewal project for Hyde Park</a>, which profoundly affected both the neighborhood's architecture and street plan.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university experienced its share of student unrest during the 1960s, beginning in 1962, when students occupied President George Beadle's office in a protest over the university's off-campus rental policies. In 1969, more than 400 students, angry about the dismissal of a popular professor, <a href="/wiki/Marlene_Dixon" title="Marlene Dixon" class="mw-redirect">Marlene Dixon</a>, occupied the Administration Building for two weeks. After the sit-in ended, when Dixon turned down a one-year reappointment, 42 students were expelled and 81 were suspended,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> the most severe response to student occupations of any American university during the student movement.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 1978, <a href="/wiki/Hanna_Holborn_Gray" title="Hanna Holborn Gray">Hanna Holborn Gray</a>, then the provost and acting president of <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>, became President of the University of Chicago, a position she held for 15 years.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Harper_Midway_Chicago.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Harper_Midway_Chicago.jpg/230px-Harper_Midway_Chicago.jpg" width="230" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Harper_Midway_Chicago.jpg/345px-Harper_Midway_Chicago.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Harper_Midway_Chicago.jpg/460px-Harper_Midway_Chicago.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Harper_Midway_Chicago.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> View from the Midway Plaisance
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s.E2.80.932010s">1990s?2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1990s?2010s">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 1999, then-President <a href="/wiki/Hugo_F._Sonnenschein" title="Hugo F. Sonnenschein">Hugo Sonnenschein</a> announced plans to relax the university's famed <a href="/wiki/Core_curriculum" title="Core curriculum" class="mw-redirect">core curriculum</a>, reducing the number of required courses from 21 to 15. When <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i>, and other major news outlets picked up this story, the university became the focal point of a national debate on education. The changes were ultimately implemented, but the controversy played a role in Sonnenschein's decision to resign in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-corewar_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-corewar-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the past decade, the university began a number of multi-million dollar expansion projects. In 2008, the University of Chicago announced plans to establish the <a href="/wiki/Milton_Friedman_Institute" title="Milton Friedman Institute" class="mw-redirect">Milton Friedman Institute</a> which attracted both support and controversy from faculty members and <span class="nowrap">students.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-petition_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-petition-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></span> The institute will cost around $200 million and occupy the buildings of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Theological_Seminary" title="Chicago Theological Seminary">Chicago Theological Seminary</a>. During the same year, investor <a href="/wiki/David_G._Booth" title="David G. Booth">David G. Booth</a> donated $300&nbsp;million to the university's <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Booth_School_of_Business" title="University of Chicago Booth School of Business" class="mw-redirect">Booth School of Business</a>, which is the largest gift in the university's history and the largest gift ever to any business school.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, planning or construction on several new buildings, half of which cost $100 million or more, was underway.<sup id="cite_ref-construction_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-construction-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Since 2009, a two-billion dollar campaign has brought substantial expansion to the campus, including the unveiling of the <a href="/wiki/Max_Palevsky_Residential_Commons" title="Max Palevsky Residential Commons" class="mw-redirect">Max Palevsky Residential Commons</a>, the South Campus Residence Hall, the <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ratner_Athletics_Center" title="Gerald Ratner Athletics Center">Gerald Ratner Athletics Center</a>, a new hospital, and a new science building. Since 2011, major construction projects have included the Jules and Gwen Knapp Center for Biomedical Discovery, a ten-story medical research center, and further additions to the medical campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Medical_Center" title="University of Chicago Medical Center">University of Chicago Medical Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-knapp_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-knapp-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:207px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Mitchell-Magdalen_comparison.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Mitchell-Magdalen_comparison.jpg/205px-Mitchell-Magdalen_comparison.jpg" width="205" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Mitchell-Magdalen_comparison.jpg/308px-Mitchell-Magdalen_comparison.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Mitchell-Magdalen_comparison.jpg/410px-Mitchell-Magdalen_comparison.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Mitchell-Magdalen_comparison.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Many older buildings of the University of Chicago employ 
        <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_Gothic" title="Collegiate Gothic" class="mw-redirect">Collegiate Gothic</a> architecture like that of the University of Oxford. For example, Chicago's Mitchell Tower (left) was modeled after Oxford's 
        <a href="/wiki/Magdalen_Tower,_Oxford" title="Magdalen Tower, Oxford" class="mw-redirect">Magdalen Tower</a> (right).
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1057px;"> 
      <div class="thumbinner"> 
       <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:UniversityofChicagoPanoramic.jpg" class="image" title="The campus of the University of Chicago. From the top of Rockefeller Chapel, the Main Quadrangles can be seen on the left (West), the Oriental Institute and the Chicago Theological Seminary can be seen in the center (North), and the Booth School of Business and Laboratory Schools can be seen on the right (East). The panoramic is bounded on both sides by the Midway Plaisance (South)."><img alt="The campus of the University of Chicago." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/49/UniversityofChicagoPanoramic.jpg/1049px-UniversityofChicagoPanoramic.jpg" width="1049" height="199" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/49/UniversityofChicagoPanoramic.jpg/1574px-UniversityofChicagoPanoramic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/49/UniversityofChicagoPanoramic.jpg/2098px-UniversityofChicagoPanoramic.jpg 2x" /></a>
       </div> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UniversityofChicagoPanoramic.jpg" title="Enlarge"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6b/Magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" /></a>
        </div> The campus of the University of Chicago. From the top of 
        <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Chapel" title="Rockefeller Chapel">Rockefeller Chapel</a>, the Main Quadrangles can be seen on the left (West), the 
        <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Institute,_Chicago" title="Oriental Institute, Chicago" class="mw-redirect">Oriental Institute</a> and the 
        <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Theological_Seminary" title="Chicago Theological Seminary">Chicago Theological Seminary</a> can be seen in the center (North), and the 
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Booth_School_of_Business" title="University of Chicago Booth School of Business" class="mw-redirect">Booth School of Business</a> and 
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Laboratory_Schools" title="University of Chicago Laboratory Schools">Laboratory Schools</a> can be seen on the right (East). The panoramic is bounded on both sides by the 
        <a href="/wiki/Midway_Plaisance" title="Midway Plaisance">Midway Plaisance</a> (South).
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The main campus of the University of Chicago consists of 211 acres (85.4&nbsp;ha) in the Chicago neighborhoods of <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_Chicago" title="Hyde Park, Chicago">Hyde Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Woodlawn,_Chicago" title="Woodlawn, Chicago">Woodlawn</a>, seven miles (11&nbsp;km) south of <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Loop" title="Chicago Loop">downtown Chicago</a>. The northern and southern portions of campus are separated by the <a href="/wiki/Midway_Plaisance" title="Midway Plaisance">Midway Plaisance</a>, a large, linear park created for the 1893 <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Columbian_Exposition" title="World's Columbian Exposition">World's Columbian Exposition</a>.</p> 
     <p>The first buildings of the University of Chicago campus, which make up what is now known as the Main Quadrangles, were part of a &quot;master plan&quot; conceived by two University of Chicago trustees and plotted by Chicago architect <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ives_Cobb" title="Henry Ives Cobb">Henry Ives Cobb</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-famousbldgs_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-famousbldgs-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> The Main Quadrangles consist of six <a href="/wiki/Quadrangle_(architecture)" title="Quadrangle (architecture)">quadrangles</a>, each surrounded by buildings, bordering one larger quadrangle.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> The buildings of the Main Quadrangles were designed by Cobb, <a href="/wiki/Shepley,_Rutan_and_Coolidge" title="Shepley, Rutan and Coolidge">Shepley, Rutan and Coolidge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holabird_%26_Roche" title="Holabird &amp; Roche" class="mw-redirect">Holabird &amp; Roche</a>, and other architectural firms in a mixture of the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_Gothic" title="Victorian Gothic" class="mw-redirect">Victorian Gothic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_Gothic" title="Collegiate Gothic" class="mw-redirect">Collegiate Gothic</a> styles, patterned on the colleges of the University of Oxford.<sup id="cite_ref-famousbldgs_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-famousbldgs-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> (Mitchell Tower, for example, is modeled after Oxford's <a href="/wiki/Magdalen_Tower,_Oxford" title="Magdalen Tower, Oxford" class="mw-redirect">Magdalen Tower</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-mitchell_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mitchell-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> and the university Commons, <a href="/wiki/Hutchinson_Hall" title="Hutchinson Hall">Hutchinson Hall</a>, replicates <a href="/wiki/Christ_Church,_Oxford" title="Christ Church, Oxford">Christ Church</a> Hall.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup>)</p> 
     <p>After the 1940s, the Gothic style on campus began to give way to self-consciously modern styles.<sup id="cite_ref-famousbldgs_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-famousbldgs-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1955, <a href="/wiki/Eero_Saarinen" title="Eero Saarinen">Eero Saarinen</a> was contracted to develop a second master plan, which led to the construction of buildings both north and south of the Midway, including the Laird Bell Law Quadrangle (a complex designed by Saarinen);<sup id="cite_ref-famousbldgs_45-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-famousbldgs-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> a series of arts buildings;<sup id="cite_ref-famousbldgs_45-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-famousbldgs-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> a building designed by <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Mies_van_der_Rohe" title="Ludwig Mies van der Rohe">Ludwig Mies van der Rohe</a> for the university's School of Social Service Administration;,<sup id="cite_ref-famousbldgs_45-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-famousbldgs-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> a building which is to become the home of the <a href="/wiki/Harris_School_of_Public_Policy_Studies" title="Harris School of Public Policy Studies">Harris School of Public Policy Studies</a> by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Durrell_Stone" title="Edward Durrell Stone" class="mw-redirect">Edward Durrell Stone</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Regenstein_Library" title="Regenstein Library">Regenstein Library</a>, the largest building on campus, a <a href="/wiki/Brutalist_architecture" title="Brutalist architecture">brutalist</a> structure designed by <a href="/wiki/Walter_Netsch" title="Walter Netsch">Walter Netsch</a> of the Chicago firm <a href="/wiki/Skidmore,_Owings_and_Merrill" title="Skidmore, Owings and Merrill">Skidmore, Owings and Merrill</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Another master plan, designed in 1999 and updated in 2004,<sup id="cite_ref-twentytwenty_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twentytwenty-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> produced the <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ratner_Athletics_Center" title="Gerald Ratner Athletics Center">Gerald Ratner Athletics Center</a> (2003),<sup id="cite_ref-twentytwenty_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twentytwenty-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Max_Palevsky_Residential_Commons" title="Max Palevsky Residential Commons" class="mw-redirect">Max Palevsky Residential Commons</a> (2001),<sup id="cite_ref-famousbldgs_45-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-famousbldgs-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_Campus_Residence_Hall" title="South Campus Residence Hall" class="mw-redirect">South Campus Residence Hall</a> and dining commons (2009), a new children's hospital,<sup id="cite_ref-milestones_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-milestones-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> and other construction, expansions, and restorations.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, the university completed the glass dome-shaped <a href="/wiki/Joe_and_Rika_Mansueto_Library" title="Joe and Rika Mansueto Library" class="mw-redirect">Joe and Rika Mansueto Library</a>, which provides a grand reading room for the university library and eliminates the need for an off-campus book depository.</p> 
     <p>The site of <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Pile-1" title="Chicago Pile-1">Chicago Pile-1</a> is a <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">National Historic Landmark</a> and is marked by the <a href="/wiki/Henry_Moore" title="Henry Moore">Henry Moore</a> sculpture <i><a href="/wiki/Nuclear_Energy_(sculpture)" title="Nuclear Energy (sculpture)">Nuclear Energy</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robie_House" title="Robie House">Robie House</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lloyd_Wright" title="Frank Lloyd Wright">Frank Lloyd Wright</a> building acquired by the university in 1963, is also a National Historic Landmark,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> as is room 405 of the <a href="/wiki/George_Herbert_Jones_Laboratory" title="George Herbert Jones Laboratory">George Herbert Jones Laboratory</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Glenn_T._Seaborg" title="Glenn T. Seaborg">Glenn T. Seaborg</a> and his team were the first to isolate plutonium.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hitchcock_Hall" title="Hitchcock Hall" class="mw-redirect">Hitchcock Hall</a>, an undergraduate dormitory, is on the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nrhp_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nrhp-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Satellite_campuses">Satellite campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Satellite campuses">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of Chicago also maintains facilities apart from its main campus. The university's <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Booth_School_of_Business" title="University of Chicago Booth School of Business" class="mw-redirect">Booth School of Business</a> maintains campuses in <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, London, and the downtown <a href="/wiki/Streeterville" title="Streeterville">Streeterville</a> neighborhood of Chicago. The Center in Paris, a campus located on the <a href="/wiki/Rive_Gauche" title="Rive Gauche" class="mw-redirect">left bank</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Seine" title="Seine">Seine</a> in Paris, hosts various undergraduate and graduate study programs.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of Chicago also opened a center in Beijing in fall 2010.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration_and_finances">Administration and finances</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Administration and finances">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The University of Chicago is governed by a board of trustees. The Board of Trustees oversees the long-term development and plans of the university and manages fundraising efforts, and is composed of 50 members including the university President.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> Directly beneath the President are the Provost, fourteen Vice Presidents (including the Chief Financial Officer, <a href="/wiki/Chief_Investment_Officer" title="Chief Investment Officer" class="mw-redirect">Chief Investment Officer</a>, and Dean of Students of the university), the Directors of <a href="/wiki/Argonne_National_Laboratory" title="Argonne National Laboratory">Argonne National Laboratory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fermilab" title="Fermilab">Fermilab</a>, the Secretary of the university, and the Student <a href="/wiki/Ombudsman" title="Ombudsman">Ombudsperson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-orgchart_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orgchart-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> As of August 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Chairman of the Board of Trustees is <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Alper" title="Andrew Alper">Andrew Alper</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> and the President of the university is <a href="/wiki/Robert_Zimmer" title="Robert Zimmer">Robert Zimmer</a>.</p> 
     <p>The university's endowment was the 13th largest among American educational institutions and state university systems in 2012<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> and as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> is valued at $6.571 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-endowment1_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-endowment1-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <table class="infobox vcard" style="width: 22em"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr>

        <td>10</td>

      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>The academic bodies of the University of Chicago consist of the <a href="/wiki/College_of_the_University_of_Chicago" title="College of the University of Chicago">College</a>, four divisions of graduate research, six professional schools, and the <a href="/wiki/Graham_School_of_Continuing_Liberal_and_Professional_Studies" title="Graham School of Continuing Liberal and Professional Studies">Graham School of Continuing Liberal and Professional Studies</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Continuing_education" title="Continuing education">continuing education</a> school). The university also contains a library system, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Press" title="University of Chicago Press">University of Chicago Press</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Laboratory_Schools" title="University of Chicago Laboratory Schools">University of Chicago Laboratory Schools</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Medical_Center" title="University of Chicago Medical Center">University of Chicago Medical Center</a>, and holds ties with a number of independent academic institutions, including <a href="/wiki/Fermilab" title="Fermilab">Fermilab</a> and <a href="/wiki/Argonne_National_Laboratory" title="Argonne National Laboratory">Argonne National Laboratory</a>. The university is accredited by <a href="/wiki/The_Higher_Learning_Commission" title="The Higher Learning Commission">The Higher Learning Commission</a> of the <a href="/wiki/North_Central_Association_of_Colleges_and_Schools" title="North Central Association of Colleges and Schools">North Central Association of Colleges and Schools</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-collegenavigator_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-collegenavigator-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university runs on a <a href="/wiki/Quarter_system" title="Quarter system" class="mw-redirect">quarter system</a> in which the academic year is divided into four terms: Summer (June?August), Autumn (September?December), Winter (January?March), and Spring (April?June).<sup id="cite_ref-calendar_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-calendar-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Full-time undergraduate students take three to four courses every quarter<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> for approximately eleven weeks before their quarterly academic breaks. The school year typically begins in late September and ends in mid-June.<sup id="cite_ref-calendar_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-calendar-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Undergraduate_college">Undergraduate college</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Undergraduate college">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/College_of_the_University_of_Chicago" title="College of the University of Chicago">College of the University of Chicago</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The College of the University of Chicago grants Bachelor of Arts and Bachelor of Science degrees in 50 <a href="/wiki/Academic_major" title="Academic major">academic majors</a><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> and 28 minors.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> The college's academics are divided into five divisions: the Biological Sciences Collegiate Division, the Physical Sciences Collegiate Division, the Social Sciences Collegiate Division, the Humanities Collegiate Division, and the New Collegiate Division.<sup id="cite_ref-collegiatedivisions_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-collegiatedivisions-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> The first four are sections within their corresponding graduate divisions, while the New Collegiate Division administers interdisciplinary majors and studies which do not fit in one of the other four divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-ncd_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ncd-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Undergraduate students are required to take a distribution of courses to satisfy the university's <a href="/wiki/Core_curriculum" title="Core curriculum" class="mw-redirect">core curriculum</a> known as the Common Core. In 2012-2013, the Core classes at Chicago were limited to 17&nbsp;students, and are generally led by a full-time professor (as opposed to a <a href="/wiki/Teaching_assistant" title="Teaching assistant">teaching assistant</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-curriculum2_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curriculum2-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> As of the 2009?2010 school year, 15&nbsp;courses, tested proficiency in a foreign language, passage of a swim test, and up to three physical education courses (depending on results of an entrance examination) are required under the Core.<sup id="cite_ref-core_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-core-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Undergraduate courses at the University of Chicago are known for their demanding standards, heavy workload and academic difficulty; according to <i><a href="/wiki/Uni_in_the_USA" title="Uni in the USA">Uni in the USA</a></i>, &quot;Among the academic cream of American universities ? Harvard, Yale, Princeton, MIT, and the University of Chicago ? it is UChicago that can most convincingly claim to provide the most rigorous, intense learning experience.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Eckhart_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Eckhart_Hall.jpg/200px-Eckhart_Hall.jpg" width="200" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Eckhart_Hall.jpg/300px-Eckhart_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Eckhart_Hall.jpg/400px-Eckhart_Hall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Eckhart_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Eckhart Hall houses the university's math and statistics departments.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Graduate_schools_and_committees">Graduate schools and committees</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Graduate schools and committees">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university graduate schools and committees are divided into four divisions: Biological Sciences, Humanities, Physical Sciences, and Social Sciences. In the spring quarter of 2009, the university enrolled 3,633 graduate students: 485 in the Biological Sciences Division, 1,076 in the Humanities Division, 732 in the Physical Sciences Division, and 1,340 in the Social Sciences Division.<sup id="cite_ref-spr09enrollmentstats_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spr09enrollmentstats-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university is home to several committees for interdisciplinary scholarship, including the <a href="/wiki/Committee_on_Social_Thought" title="Committee on Social Thought">Committee on Social Thought</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_schools">Professional schools</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Professional schools">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university contains six professional schools: the <a href="/wiki/Pritzker_School_of_Medicine" title="Pritzker School of Medicine">Pritzker School of Medicine</a> (which is a part of the Biological Sciences Division), the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Booth_School_of_Business" title="University of Chicago Booth School of Business" class="mw-redirect">Booth School of Business</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Law_School" title="University of Chicago Law School">Law School</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Divinity_School" title="University of Chicago Divinity School">Divinity School</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Harris_School_of_Public_Policy_Studies" title="Harris School of Public Policy Studies">Harris School of Public Policy Studies</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_School_of_Social_Service_Administration" title="University of Chicago School of Social Service Administration">School of Social Service Administration</a> (SSA). The total enrollment for these six professional schools was 5,086 students in the 2009 spring quarter: 2,878 students in the business school, 344 in the Divinity School, 452 in the medical school, 269 in the Harris School, 494 in SSA, and 649 in the Law School.<sup id="cite_ref-spr09enrollmentstats_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spr09enrollmentstats-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Law School is accredited by the <a href="/wiki/American_Bar_Association" title="American Bar Association">American Bar Association</a>, the Divinity School is accredited by the Commission on Accrediting of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Theological_Schools_in_the_United_States_and_Canada" title="Association of Theological Schools in the United States and Canada">Association of Theological Schools in the United States and Canada</a>, Pritzker is accredited by the <a href="/wiki/Liaison_Committee_on_Medical_Education" title="Liaison Committee on Medical Education">Liaison Committee on Medical Education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-collegenavigator_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-collegenavigator-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Associated_academic_institutions">Associated academic institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Associated academic institutions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:LB2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1a/LB2.JPG/200px-LB2.JPG" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1a/LB2.JPG/300px-LB2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1a/LB2.JPG/400px-LB2.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:LB2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The University of Chicago Lab Schools, a private day school run by the university
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university runs a number of academic institutions and programs apart from its undergraduate and postgraduate schools. It operates the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Laboratory_Schools" title="University of Chicago Laboratory Schools">University of Chicago Laboratory Schools</a> (a private <a href="/wiki/Day_school" title="Day school">day school</a> for K-12 students and <a href="/wiki/Day_care" title="Day care">day care</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-lab_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lab-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Sonia_Shankman_Orthogenic_School" title="Sonia Shankman Orthogenic School">Sonia Shankman Orthogenic School</a> (a residential treatment program for those with behavioral and emotional problems),<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> and four public <a href="/wiki/Charter_school" title="Charter school">charter schools</a> on the <a href="/wiki/South_Side_(Chicago)" title="South Side (Chicago)" class="mw-redirect">South Side</a> of Chicago administered by the university's Urban Education Institute.<sup id="cite_ref-charter_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, the Hyde Park Day School, a school for students with learning disabilities, maintains a location on the University of Chicago campus.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 1983, the University of Chicago has maintained the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_School_Mathematics_Project" title="University of Chicago School Mathematics Project">University of Chicago School Mathematics Project</a>, a mathematics program used in urban primary and secondary schools.<sup id="cite_ref-ucsmp_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ucsmp-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> The university runs a program called the Council on Advanced Studies in the Social Sciences and Humanities, which administers interdisciplinary workshops to provide a forum for graduate students, faculty, and visiting scholars to present scholarly work in progress.<sup id="cite_ref-CAS_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CAS-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> The university also operates the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Press" title="University of Chicago Press">University of Chicago Press</a>, the largest <a href="/wiki/University_press" title="University press" class="mw-redirect">university press</a> in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-press_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-press-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Regenstein_Library_entrance2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Regenstein_Library_entrance2.jpg/250px-Regenstein_Library_entrance2.jpg" width="250" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Regenstein_Library_entrance2.jpg/375px-Regenstein_Library_entrance2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Regenstein_Library_entrance2.jpg/500px-Regenstein_Library_entrance2.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Regenstein_Library_entrance2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Joseph 
        <a href="/wiki/Regenstein_Library" title="Regenstein Library">Regenstein Library</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Library_system">Library system</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Library system">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Library" title="University of Chicago Library">University of Chicago Library</a> system encompasses six libraries<sup id="cite_ref-libabout_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-libabout-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> that contain a total of 8.5&nbsp;million volumes, the 12th most among library systems in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Biglibrarylist_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Biglibrarylist-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> The largest of the university's libraries is the <a href="/wiki/Regenstein_Library" title="Regenstein Library">Regenstein Library</a>, which is the largest collection of print volumes in the United States, completed in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-biggestlibrary_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biggestlibrary-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/John_Crerar_Library" title="John Crerar Library">John Crerar Library</a> contains more than 1.3&nbsp;million volumes in the biological, medical and physical sciences and collections in general science and the philosophy and history of science, medicine, and technology.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> The university also operates a number of special libraries, including the D'Angelo Law Library, the Social Service Administration Library, and the Eckhart Library for mathematics and computer science.<sup id="cite_ref-petersons_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-petersons-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Fermilab.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Fermilab.jpg/225px-Fermilab.jpg" width="225" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Fermilab.jpg/338px-Fermilab.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Fermilab.jpg/450px-Fermilab.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Fermilab.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Aerial view of 
        <a href="/wiki/Fermilab" title="Fermilab">Fermilab</a>, one of the science research laboratories partially operated by the University of Chicago
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In fiscal year 2006, the University of Chicago spent US$305,301,000 on scientific research.<sup id="cite_ref-nsfresearch_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsfresearch-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> It is classified by the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Foundation_for_the_Advancement_of_Teaching" title="Carnegie Foundation for the Advancement of Teaching">Carnegie Foundation for the Advancement of Teaching</a> as an institution with &quot;very high research activity&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-carnegie_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carnegie-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> and is a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Committee_on_Institutional_Cooperation" title="Committee on Institutional Cooperation">Committee on Institutional Cooperation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>.</p> 
     <p>The university operates 12 research institutes and 113 research centers on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> Among these are the <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Institute,_Chicago" title="Oriental Institute, Chicago" class="mw-redirect">Oriental Institute</a>?a museum and research center for <a href="/wiki/Near_East" title="Near East">Near Eastern</a> studies owned and operated by the university?and a number of <a href="/wiki/National_Resource_Center" title="National Resource Center">National Resource Centers</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Middle_Eastern_Studies_at_the_University_of_Chicago" title="Center for Middle Eastern Studies at the University of Chicago">Center for Middle Eastern Studies</a>. Chicago also operates or is affiliated with a number of research institutions apart from the university proper. The university partially manages <a href="/wiki/Argonne_National_Laboratory" title="Argonne National Laboratory">Argonne National Laboratory</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy" title="United States Department of Energy">United States Department of Energy</a>'s national laboratory system, and has a joint stake in <a href="/wiki/Fermilab" title="Fermilab">Fermilab</a>, a nearby particle physics laboratory, as well as a stake in the <a href="/wiki/Apache_Point_Observatory" title="Apache Point Observatory">Apache Point Observatory</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sunspot,_New_Mexico" title="Sunspot, New Mexico">Sunspot, New Mexico</a>. Faculty and students at the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Technological_Institute_at_Chicago" title="Toyota Technological Institute at Chicago">Toyota Technological Institute at Chicago</a> collaborate with the university,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2013, the University announced that it was affiliating the formerly independent <a href="/wiki/Marine_Biological_Laboratory" title="Marine Biological Laboratory">Marine Biological Laboratory</a> in Woods Hole, Mass.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> Although formally unrelated, the <a href="/wiki/National_Opinion_Research_Center" title="National Opinion Research Center">National Opinion Research Center</a> is located on Chicago's campus.</p> 
     <p>The University of Chicago has been the site of some important experiments and academic movements. In economics, the university has played an important role in shaping ideas about the <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free market</a><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> and is the namesake of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_school_of_economics" title="Chicago school of economics">Chicago school of economics</a>, the school of economic thought supported by <a href="/wiki/Milton_Friedman" title="Milton Friedman">Milton Friedman</a> and other economists. The university's <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">sociology</a> department was the first independent sociology department in the United States and gave birth to the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_school_(sociology)" title="Chicago school (sociology)">Chicago school of sociology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> In physics, the university was the site of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Pile-1" title="Chicago Pile-1">Chicago Pile-1</a> (the first self-sustained man-made nuclear reaction, part of the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Project" title="Manhattan Project">Manhattan Project</a>), of <a href="/wiki/Robert_Millikan" title="Robert Millikan" class="mw-redirect">Robert Millikan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Oil-drop_experiment" title="Oil-drop experiment" class="mw-redirect">oil-drop experiment</a> that calculated the charge of the electron,<sup id="cite_ref-oildrop_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oildrop-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> and of the development of <a href="/wiki/Radiocarbon_dating" title="Radiocarbon dating">radiocarbon dating</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Chicago_USA3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="University of Chicago USA3.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/University_of_Chicago_USA3.jpg/220px-University_of_Chicago_USA3.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/University_of_Chicago_USA3.jpg/330px-University_of_Chicago_USA3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/University_of_Chicago_USA3.jpg/440px-University_of_Chicago_USA3.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Chicago_USA3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://arts.uchicago.edu/">UChicago Arts</a> joins academic departments and programs in the Division of the Humanities and the College, as well as professional organizations including <a href="/wiki/Court_Theatre_(Chicago)" title="Court Theatre (Chicago)">Court Theatre (Chicago)</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Oriental_Institute" title="University of Chicago Oriental Institute">University of Chicago Oriental Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smart_Museum_of_Art" title="Smart Museum of Art">Smart Museum of Art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Society" title="Renaissance Society">Renaissance Society</a>, University of Chicago Presents, and student arts organizations. The university has an artist-in-residence program and scholars in performance studies, contemporary art criticism, and film history. It has offered a doctorate in music composition since 1933 and in cinema &amp; media studies since 2000, a master of fine arts in visual arts (early 1970s), and a master of arts in the humanities with a creative writing track (2000). It has well-established bachelor?s degree programs in visual arts, music, and art history, and, more recently, cinema &amp; media studies (1996) and theater &amp; performance studies (2002). The College?s general education core includes a ?dramatic, music, and visual arts? requirement, inviting students to study the history of the arts, stage desire, or begin working with sculpture. Several thousand major and non-major undergraduates enroll annually in creative and performing arts classes.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://arts.uchicago.edu/content/logan-center">The Reva and David Logan Center for the Arts</a> had its grand opening, the Logan Launch Festival, in October 2012 and was built five years after David Logan, AB'39, JD'41, and his wife Reva Logan gave their record gift of $35 million. The Logan Center for the Arts, with eleven stories and 184,000 square feet of mixed-use space, features a performance hall, a studio theater, a &quot;black box&quot; theater, a film screening room, a performance penthouse, seminar style classrooms, exhibition space, music practice rooms, ensemble rehearsal rooms, performance labs, a digital media center including editing suites and a film/video production studio, and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://arts.uchicago.edu/content/caf%C3%A9-logan">Caf&eacute; Logan</a>, a cafe on the first floor that serves sandwiches, salads, wraps, and small plates.</p> 
     <p>For more history, see <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_University_of_Chicago#Arts_at_Chicago" title="History of the University of Chicago">History of the Arts at the University of Chicago</a></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: People">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Chicago_people" title="List of University of Chicago people">List of University of Chicago people</a>&nbsp;and 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_affiliated_with_the_University_of_Chicago" title="List of Nobel laureates affiliated with the University of Chicago">List of Nobel laureates affiliated with the University of Chicago</a>
     </div> 
     <p>There have been 87&nbsp;Nobel Laureates affiliated with the University of Chicago,<sup id="cite_ref-uchicago1_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uchicago1-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> 17 of whom were pursuing research or on faculty at the university at the time of the award announcement.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In addition, many Chicago alumni and scholars have won the <a href="/wiki/Fulbright_Program" title="Fulbright Program">Fulbright awards</a><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> and 49 have matriculated as <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarship" title="Rhodes Scholarship">Rhodes Scholars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <table style="text-align:center; float:right; font-size:85%; margin-left:2em; margin:auto;" class="wikitable">
