     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_body">Student body</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Student body">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In the 2012 Spring Quarter, the University of Chicago enrolled 5,122 students in the College, 3444 students in its four graduate divisions, 5020 students in its professional schools, and 14,013 students overall.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2012 Spring Quarter, <a href="/wiki/International_student" title="International student">international students</a> comprised almost 19% of the overall study body, over 26% of students were domestic ethnic minorities,<sup id="cite_ref-spring09stats_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spring09stats-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> and about 44% of enrolled students were female.<sup id="cite_ref-SPRING_QUARTER_2012_STATISTICAL_REPORT_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPRING_QUARTER_2012_STATISTICAL_REPORT-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> The middle 50% band of <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> scores for the undergraduate class of 2015, excluding the writing section, was 1420?1530,<sup id="cite_ref-Profile_for_the_Class_of_2015_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Profile_for_the_Class_of_2015-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> the average <a href="/wiki/MCAT" title="MCAT" class="mw-redirect">MCAT</a> score for entering students in the Pritzker School of Medicine in 2011 was 36,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> and the median <a href="/wiki/LSAT" title="LSAT" class="mw-redirect">LSAT</a> score for entering students in the Law School in 2011 was 171.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alumni">Alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Alumni">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Chicago_alumni" title="List of University of Chicago alumni">List of University of Chicago alumni</a>
     </div> 
     <p>In 2004, the University of Chicago claimed 133,155 living alumni.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Notable alumni in the field of government and politics include community organizer <a href="/wiki/Saul_Alinsky" title="Saul Alinsky">Saul Alinsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Obama</a> campaign advisor <a href="/wiki/David_Axelrod" title="David Axelrod">David Axelrod</a>, <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_of_the_United_States" title="Attorney General of the United States" class="mw-redirect">Attorney General</a> and federal judge <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bork" title="Robert Bork">Robert Bork</a>, <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_of_the_United_States" title="Attorney General of the United States" class="mw-redirect">Attorney General</a> <a href="/wiki/Ramsay_Clark" title="Ramsay Clark" class="mw-redirect">Ramsay Clark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_Jersey" title="Governor of New Jersey">Governor of New Jersey</a> <a href="/wiki/Jon_Corzine" title="Jon Corzine">Jon Corzine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prohibition_in_the_United_States" title="Prohibition in the United States">Prohibition</a> agent <a href="/wiki/Eliot_Ness" title="Eliot Ness">Eliot Ness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court</a> Justice <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Stevens" title="John Paul Stevens">John Paul Stevens</a>, prime minister of Canada <a href="/wiki/William_Lyon_Mackenzie_King" title="William Lyon Mackenzie King">William Lyon Mackenzie King</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> President <a href="/wiki/Paul_Wolfowitz" title="Paul Wolfowitz">Paul Wolfowitz</a>,former minister of economy and finance in Haiti <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Delatour" title="Leslie Delatour">Leslie Delatour</a>.</p> 
     <p>In business, <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a> and <a href="/wiki/MF_Global" title="MF Global">MF Global</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Jon_Corzine" title="Jon Corzine">Jon Corzine</a>, Arley D. Cathey, <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_L.P." title="Bloomberg L.P.">Bloomberg L.P.</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Doctoroff" title="Daniel Doctoroff" class="mw-redirect">Daniel Doctoroff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Credit_Suisse" title="Credit Suisse">Credit Suisse</a> CEO <a href="/wiki/Brady_Dougan" title="Brady Dougan">Brady Dougan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morningstar,_Inc." title="Morningstar, Inc.">Morningstar, Inc.</a> founder and CEO <a href="/wiki/Joe_Mansueto" title="Joe Mansueto">Joe Mansueto</a>, and businessman and author <a href="/wiki/Dick_Stoken" title="Dick Stoken">Dick Stoken</a> are all alumni.</p> 
     <p>In journalism, notable graduates include <a href="/wiki/New_York_Times" title="New York Times" class="mw-redirect">New York Times</a> columnist <a href="/wiki/David_Brooks_(journalist)" title="David Brooks (journalist)">David Brooks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_Post" title="Washington Post" class="mw-redirect">Washington Post</a> columnist <a href="/wiki/David_S._Broder" title="David S. Broder">David Broder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_Post" title="Washington Post" class="mw-redirect">Washington Post</a> publisher <a href="/wiki/Katharine_Graham" title="Katharine Graham">Katharine Graham</a>, investigative journalist <a href="/wiki/Seymour_Hirsch" title="Seymour Hirsch" class="mw-redirect">Seymour Hirsch</a>, statistical analyst <a href="/wiki/Nate_Silver" title="Nate Silver">Nate Silver</a>, and CBS News Business and Economics Correspondent / Anchor of CBS This Morning Saturday Edition <a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Jarvis" title="Rebecca Jarvis">Rebecca Jarvis</a>.</p> 
     <p>In literature, novelists <a href="/wiki/Philip_Roth" title="Philip Roth">Philip Roth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tucker_Max" title="Tucker Max">Tucker Max</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Vonnegut" title="Kurt Vonnegut">Kurt Vonnegut</a> are graduates.</p> 
     <p>In academia, alumni include astronomer <a href="/wiki/Carl_Sagan" title="Carl Sagan">Carl Sagan</a>, economist <a href="/wiki/Milton_Friedman" title="Milton Friedman">Milton Friedman</a>, astronomer <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Hubble" title="Edwin Hubble">Edwin Hubble</a>, Africanist <a href="/wiki/Marimba_Ani" title="Marimba Ani">Marimba Ani</a> and international relations scholar <a href="/wiki/Samuel_P._Huntington" title="Samuel P. Huntington">Samuel P. Huntington</a>.</p> 
     <p>Notable former students who did not graduate include novelist <a href="/wiki/Saul_Bellow" title="Saul Bellow">Saul Bellow</a>, film critic <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oracle_Corporation" title="Oracle Corporation">Oracle Corporation</a> founder and CEO <a href="/wiki/Larry_Ellison" title="Larry Ellison">Larry Ellison</a>, and director <a href="/wiki/Mike_Nichols" title="Mike Nichols">Mike Nichols</a>.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Maroons" title="Chicago Maroons">Chicago Maroons</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:190px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UChicago_Maroons.svg" class="image"><img alt="UChicago Maroons.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cc/UChicago_Maroons.svg/188px-UChicago_Maroons.svg.png" width="188" height="117" class="thumbimage" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"></div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Chicago hosts 19 varsity sports teams: 10 men's teams and 9 women's teams,<sup id="cite_ref-sportsfacts_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sportsfacts-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> all called the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Maroons" title="Chicago Maroons">Maroons</a>, with 585 students participating in the 2008?2009 school year.<sup id="cite_ref-sportsfacts_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sportsfacts-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Maroons compete in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA" class="mw-redirect">NCAA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Division_III_(NCAA)" title="Division III (NCAA)">Division III</a> as members of the <a href="/wiki/University_Athletic_Association" title="University Athletic Association">University Athletic Association</a> (UAA). The university was a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a> and participated in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA" class="mw-redirect">NCAA</a> Division I Men's Basketball and Football and was a regular participant in the Men's Basketball tournament. In 1935 the University of Chicago reached the Sweet Sixteen.<sup id="cite_ref-sportsfacts_115-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sportsfacts-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the university chose to withdraw from the conference in 1946 after University President <a href="/wiki/Robert_Maynard_Hutchins" title="Robert Maynard Hutchins">Robert Maynard Hutchins</a> de-emphasized varsity athletics in 1939 and dropped football.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> (In 1969, Chicago reinstated football as a Division III team, resuming playing its home games at the new <a href="/wiki/Stagg_Field" title="Stagg Field">Stagg Field</a>.)</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Reynoldsclub.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/47/Reynoldsclub.JPG/200px-Reynoldsclub.JPG" width="200" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/47/Reynoldsclub.JPG/300px-Reynoldsclub.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/47/Reynoldsclub.JPG/400px-Reynoldsclub.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Reynoldsclub.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The university's Reynolds Club, the student center
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_organizations">Student organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Student organizations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Students at the University of Chicago run over 400 clubs and organizations known as Recognized Student Organizations (RSOs).<sup id="cite_ref-activities_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-activities-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rsodatabase_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsodatabase-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> These include cultural and religious groups, academic clubs and teams, and common-interest organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-rsodatabase_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsodatabase-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> Among notable RSOs are the nation's longest continuously running student film society <a href="/wiki/Doc_Films" title="Doc Films">Doc Films</a>, organizing committee for the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Scavenger_Hunt" title="University of Chicago Scavenger Hunt">University of Chicago Scavenger Hunt</a>, the twice-weekly student newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chicago_Maroon" title="The Chicago Maroon">The Chicago Maroon</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Alternative_weekly" title="Alternative weekly" class="mw-redirect">alternative weekly</a> student newspaper the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Weekly" title="Chicago Weekly">Chicago Weekly</a></i>, the nation's second oldest continuously running student improvisational theater troupe <i><a href="/wiki/Off-Off_Campus" title="Off-Off Campus">Off-Off Campus</a></i>, and the university-owned radio station <a href="/wiki/WHPK-FM" title="WHPK-FM">WHPK-FM</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fraternities_and_sororities">Fraternities and sororities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Fraternities and sororities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>There are fourteen <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">fraternities</a> and seven <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">sororities</a> at the University of Chicago,<sup id="cite_ref-Greek_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greek-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as one co-ed community service fraternity, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Omega" title="Alpha Phi Omega">Alpha Phi Omega</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Four of the sororities are members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Panhellenic_Conference" title="National Panhellenic Conference">National Panhellenic Conference</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-frats_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frats-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> and ten of the fraternities form the University of Chicago Interfraternity Council.<sup id="cite_ref-ifc_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ifc-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2002, the Associate Director of Student Activities estimated that 8?10 percent of undergraduates were members of fraternities or sororities.<sup id="cite_ref-frats_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frats-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> The student activities office has used similar figures, stating that one in ten undergraduates participate in Greek life.<sup id="cite_ref-Greek_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greek-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_housing">Student housing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Student housing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Blue,_orange_and_pink.jpg" class="image"><img alt="An orange brick building with pink window frames and a blue roof" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Blue%2C_orange_and_pink.jpg/100px-Blue%2C_orange_and_pink.jpg" width="100" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Blue%2C_orange_and_pink.jpg/150px-Blue%2C_orange_and_pink.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Blue%2C_orange_and_pink.jpg/200px-Blue%2C_orange_and_pink.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Blue,_orange_and_pink.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Max_Palevsky_Residential_Commons" title="Max Palevsky Residential Commons" class="mw-redirect">Max Palevsky Residential Commons</a>, a dormitory constructed in 2001 designed by postmodernist Mexican architect 
        <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Legorreta" title="Ricardo Legorreta">Ricardo Legorreta</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Housing_at_the_University_of_Chicago" title="Housing at the University of Chicago">Housing at the University of Chicago</a>
     </div> 
     <p>On-campus undergraduate students at the University of Chicago participate in a <a href="/wiki/House_system" title="House system">house system</a> in which each student is assigned to one of the university's 10 <a href="/wiki/Residence_hall" title="Residence hall" class="mw-redirect">residence hall</a> buildings and to a smaller community within their residence hall called a &quot;house&quot;. There are 35 houses, with an average of 70 students in each house<sup id="cite_ref-collegehousing_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-collegehousing-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Freshmen are required to participate in the house system, and housing is guaranteed every year thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-housing2_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-housing2-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> About 60% of undergraduate students live on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-housing2_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-housing2-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>For graduate students, the university owns and operates 28 apartment buildings near campus.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a>]</span></h3>

      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Scavenger_Hunt" title="University of Chicago Scavenger Hunt">University of Chicago Scavenger Hunt</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Every May since 1987, the University of Chicago has held the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Scavenger_Hunt" title="University of Chicago Scavenger Hunt">University of Chicago Scavenger Hunt</a>, in which large teams of students compete to obtain notoriously esoteric items from a list.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 1963, the Festival of the Arts (FOTA) takes over campus for 7?10 days of exhibitions and interactive artistic endeavors.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> The university also annually holds a summer carnival and concert called <a href="/wiki/Summer_Breeze_(concert)" title="Summer Breeze (concert)">Summer Breeze</a> that hosts outside musicians, and is home to <a href="/wiki/Doc_Films" title="Doc Films">Doc Films</a>, a student film society founded in 1932 that screens films nightly at the university. Since 1946, the university has organized the <a href="/wiki/Latke-Hamantash_Debate" title="Latke-Hamantash Debate" class="mw-redirect">Latke-Hamantash Debate</a>, which involves humorous discussions about the relative merits and meanings of <a href="/wiki/Latke" title="Latke" class="mw-redirect">Latke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hamantash" title="Hamantash">Hamantash</a>.</p> 
     <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Chicago&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <ul> 
      <li id="cnote_A"><b><a href="#ref_A_1">^</a></b> &quot;Graduate school&quot; figures are totals of the data from each of the four divisions. &quot;Professional school&quot; figures are totals of Booth, the Divinity School, the Law School, Harris, SSA, and Pritzker. The Graham School of Continuing Liberal and Professional Studies, &quot;Graduate Affairs&quot;, and &quot;Special Programs&quot; are included in the &quot;university total&quot; figures, but not in anything else.</li> 
     </ul>
